It fits<span class='line-break'> </span> fine.  I think she is<span class='line-break'> </span> pleased with it.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry is [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> a bout a pen point.<span class='line-break'> </span> 8 oclock</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1832">
<h3><a name="page-1832">Friday, November 26, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim and<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Marvin stripped<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco all day.  Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> cut some wood.  Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> come a few minutes.<span class='line-break'> </span> This morning Mrs Owen<span class='line-break'> </span> sent me some meat.<span class='line-break'> </span> I cooked some of it<span class='line-break'> </span> for dinner.  Ella<span class='line-break'> </span> Hubbard come this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Jim Power<span class='line-break'> </span> come with her.  He<span class='line-break'> </span> did not stay but<span class='line-break'> </span> a few minutes.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Owen sent me <span class='line-break'> </span> some sausage to<span class='line-break'> </span> night.  I was glad<span class='line-break'> </span> to get it.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and Ben did<span class='line-break'> </span> not strip tobacco<span class='line-break'> </span> to night.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1833">
<h3><a name="page-1833">Saturday, November 27, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day.  Rain<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Ben and<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim finished stripping<span class='line-break'> </span> what tobacco they intend<span class='line-break'> </span> and put it in the pit.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben hauled a load of<span class='line-break'> </span> wood this morning and<span class='line-break'> </span> I am glad.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car and Ella Hubard<span class='line-break'> </span> and Josie shelled some<span class='line-break'> </span> beans to night.  I help<span class='line-break'> </span> a little tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin Smith lost a <span class='line-break'> </span> check today.  I do hope<span class='line-break'> </span> he may find it yet.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  Killed a<span class='line-break'> </span> chicken, made apple<span class='line-break'> </span> dumplings.  Josie <span class='line-break'> </span> made a nice salid.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1834">
<h3><a name="page-1834">Sunday, November 28, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A very rainy day.  Mrs<span class='line-break'> </span> Hubard could<span class='line-break'> </span> not go home on account<span class='line-break'> </span> of the rain.  I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> All of the folks was<span class='line-break'> </span> at home.  Seemed<span class='line-break'> </span> to enjoy dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car and I did not <span class='line-break'> </span> go down to supper<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  I wrote Effie<span class='line-break'> </span> a letter to day.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> went to see John<span class='line-break'> </span> Hutcherson this morning<span class='line-break'> </span> a bout carrieing his<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  Jim went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvins this evening.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> wanted to go but the<span class='line-break'> </span> weather was so<span class='line-break'> </span> rough I could not go.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1835">
<h3><a name="page-1835">Monday, November 29, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy bad day.  No rain.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben carried<span class='line-break'> </span> Ella Hubard to Cedar<span class='line-break'> </span> Forest.  Franklin went<span class='line-break'> </span> with him.  Jim &amp; Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> loaded John Hutchersons<span class='line-break'> </span> truck with tobacco this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  Jim went with<span class='line-break'> </span> him to South Boston.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mollie Reynols come<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  She lost her<span class='line-break'> </span> spectacles on her way<span class='line-break'> </span> here.  She went part of the<span class='line-break'> </span> way back and found them.<span class='line-break'> </span> She stoped at Carries.  Edna<span class='line-break'> </span> and I went with her.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie was makeing<span class='line-break'> </span> the girls some aprons.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Dews come<span class='line-break'> </span> to see Mrs Car<span class='line-break'> </span> a bout moveing to<span class='line-break'> </span> her place that he rented [?]</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1836">
<h3><a name="page-1836">Tuesday, November 30, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A very rainy day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben worked on his car<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  Helped<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin tie tobacco a<span class='line-break'> </span> while this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> We are out of wood.<span class='line-break'> </span> Have not got any<span class='line-break'> </span> corn shucked.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim come home <span class='line-break'> </span> from South Boston<span class='line-break'> </span> just as wet as<span class='line-break'> </span> could be.  John<span class='line-break'> </span> Hutcherson got<span class='line-break'> </span> in the creek <span class='line-break'> </span> with his truck<span class='line-break'> </span> and hiered Edward<span class='line-break'> </span> to pull him out.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am sorry for<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and cant<span class='line-break'> </span> help him and he<span class='line-break'> </span> would not let me<span class='line-break'> </span> if I could.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1837">
<h3><a name="page-1837">Wednesday, December  1, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  The land <span class='line-break'> </span> is as wet as<span class='line-break'> </span> it can be.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and Ben cut<span class='line-break'> </span> wood in the woods to<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  The Owens stopped ]?]<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco mans in [?] <span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco.  I got<span class='line-break'> </span> breakfast and milked<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; churned and got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  I cooked beans<span class='line-break'> </span> and potatoes.  This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to Marvins<span class='line-break'> </span> a while.  Carrie was<span class='line-break'> </span> sewing for the little girls.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car and Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> shelled a lot of beans.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went to <span class='line-break'> </span> school.  Henry got<span class='line-break'> </span> a letter from<span class='line-break'> </span> Evylin this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> 9:30 oclock</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1838">
<h3><a name="page-1838">Thursday, December  2, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben hauled<span class='line-break'> </span> some wood.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim helped.  Marvin striped<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco all day and Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Jim went up there tonight<span class='line-break'> </span> to tie tobacco.  Henry went<span class='line-break'> </span> to school.  Some of the boys<span class='line-break'> </span> from school went to Gretna<span class='line-break'> </span> to play basket ball.<span class='line-break'> </span> Bettie Haley washed<span class='line-break'> </span> here today.  Josie &amp; Mrs<span class='line-break'> </span> Car finished shelling<span class='line-break'> </span> the white beans today.<span class='line-break'> </span> I ironed some<span class='line-break'> </span> and got dinner<span class='line-break'> </span> as usual.  Cooked<span class='line-break'> </span> beans and potatoes.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1839">
<h3><a name="page-1839">Friday, December  3, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> hauled and sawed some wood<span class='line-break'> </span> to day.  Ben tied<span class='line-break'> </span> my calf this morning<span class='line-break'> </span> and carried her to the <span class='line-break'> </span> spring.  We will put her in<span class='line-break'> </span> the shop when it rains.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car was sick<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning and suffered<span class='line-break'> </span> very much but is<span class='line-break'> </span> better tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> I ironed some to<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  Stewed pumpkin<span class='line-break'> </span> and killed a chicken.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry did not go to<span class='line-break'> </span> school today.  He <span class='line-break'> </span> had no shoes fit to<span class='line-break'> </span> wear except his<span class='line-break'> </span> Sunday best and it <span class='line-break'> </span> was so muddy he <span class='line-break'> </span> would of ruined <span class='line-break'> </span> them [?]</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1840">
<h3><a name="page-1840">Saturday, December  4, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> sawed wood this morning<span class='line-break'> </span> then Ben carried Mrs Car<span class='line-break'> </span> home.  Come back and carried <span class='line-break'> </span> me to Mount Airy then<span class='line-break'> </span> they carried the disk home<span class='line-break'> </span> to Reynols then put the<span class='line-break'> </span> engine under shelter.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim cleaned the hog pens<span class='line-break'> </span> and put down the seat<span class='line-break'> </span> box and made him a<span class='line-break'> </span> box to put his meat in<span class='line-break'> </span> when they kill hogs.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has bin like Josie <span class='line-break'> </span> of olde today.  I am uneasy,<span class='line-break'> </span> so afraid she will do something<span class='line-break'> </span> that will hurt her.<span class='line-break'> </span> She has the baby tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin and family <span class='line-break'> </span> went to church this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Ben bought<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry a pair of shoes<span class='line-break'> </span> to day.  [?] rubber boots.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1841">
<h3><a name="page-1841">Sunday, December  5, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear windy day.  Rain<span class='line-break'> </span> last night.  Jim has<span class='line-break'> </span> staid at home all day.  He<span class='line-break'> </span> looked for Nellie &amp; Evylin.<span class='line-break'> </span> They did not come.  Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> went for Mrs Car this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  I am glad that<span class='line-break'> </span> she come with him back.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie thought of going with<span class='line-break'> </span> him but Carrie came<span class='line-break'> </span> and she did not go.<span class='line-break'> </span> Grace Brumfield &amp; Kate<span class='line-break'> </span> Harvey come.  We were<span class='line-break'> </span> glad to have them.  Glades<span class='line-break'> </span> and Doris and Janie<span class='line-break'> </span> Brumfield &amp; Christenia<span class='line-break'> </span> Reynols come a while.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin and family<span class='line-break'> </span> went to church<span class='line-break'> </span> and then Carrie &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> the little ones come<span class='line-break'> </span> to see us.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1842">
<h3><a name="page-1842">Monday, December  6, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  The boys<span class='line-break'> </span> killed hogs.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> had two to kill, Ben 4.<span class='line-break'> </span> We got up at four oclock.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin and Owen and<span class='line-break'> </span> William Gilbert helped<span class='line-break'> </span> them.  Bettie Haley<span class='line-break'> </span> helped me.  Nellie &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Viney a colored woman<span class='line-break'> </span> come at twelve oclock.<span class='line-break'> </span> They cut up the hogs and<span class='line-break'> </span> salted them up.  Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> got her sausage ground<span class='line-break'> </span> to night.  Jim and Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> helped some.  Heard to<span class='line-break'> </span> day that Lizzie write<span class='line-break'> </span> died last night.<span class='line-break'> </span> I had a letter from<span class='line-break'> </span> Mary Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> to day.  Mollie Reynolds come<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Josie went<span class='line-break'> </span> with Ben to Mount Airy.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1843">
<h3><a name="page-1843">Tuesday, December  7, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> helped Marvin kill hogs.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie put up her sausage<span class='line-break'> </span> and cut the meat for mine.  Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> seasoned for us both.  Vinie<span class='line-break'> </span> the colored woman fried out<span class='line-break'> </span> the lard for us.<span class='line-break'> </span> Reese went for Martha<span class='line-break'> </span> Miller this morning<span class='line-break'> </span> to help Carrie.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Rob Hubbard and Ella and two<span class='line-break'> </span> business men come<span class='line-break'> </span> to see Mrs Car.<span class='line-break'> </span> They did not stay <span class='line-break'> </span> for dinner.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1844">
<h3><a name="page-1844">Wednesday, December  8, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Rain last night.  Rain<span class='line-break'> </span> and hail a gain to day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Jim shucked<span class='line-break'> </span> some corn<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben carried Jim and<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie and Vinia to<span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna on their way<span class='line-break'> </span> home to Chatham.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went with them<span class='line-break'> </span> to Gretna.  I bought<span class='line-break'> </span> several little things.<span class='line-break'> </span> We left them at<span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna.  It rained <span class='line-break'> </span> and hailed all the<span class='line-break'> </span> way home but we<span class='line-break'> </span> made it ok.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie had made a <span class='line-break'> </span> fire when we<span class='line-break'> </span> got back.  She was <span class='line-break'> </span> going to get supper.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> He was so colde that he<span class='line-break'> </span> cried.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1845">
<h3><a name="page-1845">Thursday, December  9, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> The trees was covered<span class='line-break'> </span> with ice that is all gone<span class='line-break'> </span> to night.  Jim is in<span class='line-break'> </span> Chatham we think.  Ben worked<span class='line-break'> </span> on Henrys bycicle then split<span class='line-break'> </span> a little wood.  Went rabbit<span class='line-break'> </span> hunting late this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Did not kill any thing.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have bin busy all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got breakfast, milked the<span class='line-break'> </span> cows, cut up two pumpkins,<span class='line-break'> </span> put them on to cook, cleaned a <span class='line-break'> </span> hogs face, put that and haslet<span class='line-break'> </span> on to cook then got dinner<span class='line-break'> </span> then churned, put on some<span class='line-break'> </span> spar ribs to boil, watered the <span class='line-break'> </span> calf, changed the water that<span class='line-break'> </span> chidlins was in.  By that time<span class='line-break'> </span> my hogs face was done.  Picked<span class='line-break'> </span> the bones out and made scrapple.<span class='line-break'> </span> Took up my pumpkin and<span class='line-break'> </span> washed up the things that I <span class='line-break'> </span> used.  Brought in some wood.<span class='line-break'> </span> Went to the spring twice.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie got supper.  Mrs. Car and<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie washed dishes.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1846">
<h3><a name="page-1846">Friday, December 10, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to the<span class='line-break'> </span> mill this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carried all the wheat<span class='line-break'> </span> that he had boght<span class='line-break'> </span> some brand paid 2.75<span class='line-break'> </span> per bushal.  Josie made<span class='line-break'> </span> the baby a dress.<span class='line-break'> </span> I washed the baby,<span class='line-break'> </span> five aprons, and<span class='line-break'> </span> ironed them.  I have <span class='line-break'> </span> bin busy all day<span class='line-break'> </span> and nothing to<span class='line-break'> </span> show for what I have<span class='line-break'> </span> done.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben has gone to the<span class='line-break'> </span> school house to<span class='line-break'> </span> a farmers meeting.<span class='line-break'> </span> He went with <span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1847">
<h3><a name="page-1847">Saturday, December 11, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Ben,<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie, Franklin<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Mabel<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Mr Jim Power.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car went with them.<span class='line-break'> </span> She staid down there.  Mr <span class='line-break'> </span> Power was hunting.  They<span class='line-break'> </span> did not see him.<span class='line-break'> </span> Betty Haley &amp; Shooler <span class='line-break'> </span> washed here today.<span class='line-break'> </span> I washed up the<span class='line-break'> </span> kitchen.  Henry &amp; Edna<span class='line-break'> </span> helped me some.<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna and I went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Carries a few<span class='line-break'> </span> minutes this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie was sewing<span class='line-break'> </span> on my dress.<span class='line-break'> </span> I think she will<span class='line-break'> </span> finish it to night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Martha Miller went<span class='line-break'> </span> home this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben has gone to the lodge.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1848">
<h3><a name="page-1848">Sunday, December 12, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Cloudy most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> No rain yet.  Ben has<span class='line-break'> </span> bin at home<span class='line-break'> </span> all day and all of us<span class='line-break'> </span> has staid at home.  I have<span class='line-break'> </span> done all the cookin,<span class='line-break'> </span> milked the cows.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben brought in a <span class='line-break'> </span> barrel of flour <span class='line-break'> </span> and a can of oil<span class='line-break'> </span> to night.  Ben helped<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry fix up his<span class='line-break'> </span> bysicle so he can<span class='line-break'> </span> ride it.  He is beggin<span class='line-break'> </span> to ride to the<span class='line-break'> </span> school house.  I hope<span class='line-break'> </span> that they wont let<span class='line-break'> </span> him.  I started to<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvins and heard<span class='line-break'> </span> that they were not at<span class='line-break'> </span> home so I come back.  9 oclock</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1849">
<h3><a name="page-1849">Monday, December 13, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Cloudy all day.  Rain to night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben out a little <span class='line-break'> </span> to day.  He killed three<span class='line-break'> </span> sqirrels.  He dressed them.<span class='line-break'> </span> I cooked chidlins to<span class='line-break'> </span> day at the wash house.<span class='line-break'> </span> I washed some.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie washed and pressed<span class='line-break'> </span> some goods to make<span class='line-break'> </span> Franklin a suit<span class='line-break'> </span> of clothes.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim come home<span class='line-break'> </span> to night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie sent a new<span class='line-break'> </span> dress that she had<span class='line-break'> </span> made.  Sent it by<span class='line-break'> </span> William Gilbert.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Owen finished<span class='line-break'> </span> a cureing of<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Owen got my cards to make<span class='line-break'> </span> some bats for a quilt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1850">
<h3><a name="page-1850">Tuesday, December 14, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim worked on the spring.<span class='line-break'> </span> Helped it very<span class='line-break'> </span> much.  I cooked all the<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  Boiled three<span class='line-break'> </span> sqirrels and back bone,<span class='line-break'> </span> hogs face and liver.  Made<span class='line-break'> </span> scrapple, baked a tung [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie and Ben started<span class='line-break'> </span> to Danville.  I hope<span class='line-break'> </span> that they made the<span class='line-break'> </span> trip ok.  They got<span class='line-break'> </span> to Gretna allright.<span class='line-break'> </span> I talked with Grace<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  I am<span class='line-break'> </span> always glad when <span class='line-break'> </span> she answers the <span class='line-break'> </span> phone.  The baby has<span class='line-break'> </span> done very well so<span class='line-break'> </span> far.  Hope she will let me sleep<span class='line-break'> </span> some to night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim helped load the waggon<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening for Owens.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1851">
<h3><a name="page-1851">Wednesday, December 15, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> cut in the woods.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Josie was in Danville.<span class='line-break'> </span> Come home about dark.<span class='line-break'> </span> I had supper a bout<span class='line-break'> </span> ready.  Had sqirrel<span class='line-break'> </span> hash and sausage for<span class='line-break'> </span> supper.  The baby<span class='line-break'> </span> done very well last<span class='line-break'> </span> night.  Molly and<span class='line-break'> </span> [?] come a while<span class='line-break'> </span> last night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Owens carried<span class='line-break'> </span> a load of tobacco to<span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna to day.  He<span class='line-break'> </span> went on the waggon.<span class='line-break'> </span> Could not get any<span class='line-break'> </span> one to go on a truck.<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna has just broke<span class='line-break'> </span> a chamber vessel<span class='line-break'> </span> all to peices.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1852">
<h3><a name="page-1852">Thursday, December 16, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben and<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim cut in the woods to<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  Marvin hauled wood.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie baked <span class='line-break'> </span> a fruit cake this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to Marvins<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> was sewing.  I worked<span class='line-break'> </span> some button holes in<span class='line-break'> </span> Pauls waists.  Charles<span class='line-break'> </span> Harvey come there to<span class='line-break'> </span> see if he could get<span class='line-break'> </span> William Gilbert to<span class='line-break'> </span> cut wood for him.<span class='line-break'> </span> Could not get him.<span class='line-break'> </span> I brought in 14<span class='line-break'> </span> eggs to night.  Eggs<span class='line-break'> </span> is selling at [?] cts<span class='line-break'> </span> per doz.  Henry was<span class='line-break'> </span> reading in his new<span class='line-break'> </span> book to night.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children all has<span class='line-break'> </span> colds &amp; coughs.<span class='line-break'> </span> Most everyone has <span class='line-break'> </span> colds now.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1853">
<h3><a name="page-1853">Friday, December 17, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cool windy day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and Ben cut and<span class='line-break'> </span> hauled wood all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> washed the dishes<span class='line-break'> </span> and cut out a suit<span class='line-break'> </span> for Franklin.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin and William<span class='line-break'> </span> (col) went to Gretna.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went with them.<span class='line-break'> </span> We bought several things.  We made the <span class='line-break'> </span> trip fine.  Josie had<span class='line-break'> </span> supper done when<span class='line-break'> </span> I got home</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1854">
<h3><a name="page-1854">Saturday, December 18, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear cold day.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> got some wood.  Owen hoed [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> some corn.  Ben &amp; Jim [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> out some feed.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to Chatham and<span class='line-break'> </span> I went with him.  He carried<span class='line-break'> </span> some meat &amp; beans for Nellie.<span class='line-break'> </span> We did not see Evylin.  She<span class='line-break'> </span> and some girls had gone for<span class='line-break'> </span> hollie to decorate with.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> had a good letter from Denia<span class='line-break'> </span> yesterday.  She was at Earnest<span class='line-break'> </span> Craddocks.  Lottie has a new<span class='line-break'> </span> boy baby.  Today is Hazel Smiths<span class='line-break'> </span> birth day.  I did not go in a<span class='line-break'> </span> store at Chatham.  We stoped<span class='line-break'> </span> at Gretna a few minutes.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie got dinner and supper.<span class='line-break'> </span> She had supper a bout<span class='line-break'> </span> ready when we got<span class='line-break'> </span> home.  The roads is awful<span class='line-break'> </span> in some places from<span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna to Chatham.  Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Strait Stone<span class='line-break'> </span> and Mount Airy to day.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1855">
<h3><a name="page-1855">Sunday, December 19, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  All of <span class='line-break'> </span> the family staid<span class='line-break'> </span> at home until dinner<span class='line-break'> </span> except Henry.  He went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Lee Brumfields and from<span class='line-break'> </span> there to Clide Reynols.<span class='line-break'> </span> He went on his wheel<span class='line-break'> </span> to Lees.  Put in a barn<span class='line-break'> </span> and some one took it.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to George<span class='line-break'> </span> Blairs.  Did not see<span class='line-break'> </span> any of but Denia<span class='line-break'> </span> and Frank.<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna had made a <span class='line-break'> </span> fire and was going<span class='line-break'> </span> to the spring when<span class='line-break'> </span> I got home.  All<span class='line-break'> </span> the Blair girls was<span class='line-break'> </span> gone to Strait Stone<span class='line-break'> </span> and Rens.  Cordie<span class='line-break'> </span> was at Rens.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1856">
<h3><a name="page-1856">Monday, December 20, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A very good day.  Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Jim shucked<span class='line-break'> </span> corn and hauled feed all<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  I got dinner &amp; ironed<span class='line-break'> </span> a little and churned.<span class='line-break'> </span> Fixed up the butter.  Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Carries.  They<span class='line-break'> </span> made Franklin a suit<span class='line-break'> </span> I think is beautiful for them<span class='line-break'> </span> to make.  Ben carried Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> and went after her.  Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> went to school.  He got<span class='line-break'> </span> his wheel a gain.  Mr<span class='line-break'> </span> Field did not teach to<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  The patrons met<span class='line-break'> </span> to night to decide a<span class='line-break'> </span> bout his teaching after <span class='line-break'> </span> xmas.  Beatris Owen<span class='line-break'> </span> was here a while this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  The baby <span class='line-break'> </span> done fine for her<span class='line-break'> </span> while Josie was gone.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1857">
<h3><a name="page-1857">Tuesday, December 21, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> shucked corn.<span class='line-break'> </span> This morning Ben &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie went to Mount<span class='line-break'> </span> Airy.  They got home<span class='line-break'> </span> at twelve.  Jim &amp; Ben and <span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin &amp; William cut<span class='line-break'> </span> feed all the evening<span class='line-break'> </span> for Ben &amp; Marvin.<span class='line-break'> </span> I ironed some &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner.  Late in<span class='line-break'> </span> the day I went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvins.  Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> was baking her fruit<span class='line-break'> </span> cake.  It looked<span class='line-break'> </span> good.  Henry went<span class='line-break'> </span> to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna has a very<span class='line-break'> </span> bad colde.<span class='line-break'> </span> The baby cried<span class='line-break'> </span> most of the evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I spilt my ink.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1858">
<h3><a name="page-1858">Wednesday, December 22, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day and rain<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  The men folks<span class='line-break'> </span> sawed wood here this morning<span class='line-break'> </span> and at Marvins this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Irvin Harvey had the team<span class='line-break'> </span> today to haul wood.  It<span class='line-break'> </span> rained so much this evening<span class='line-break'> </span> that they could not haul<span class='line-break'> </span> much.  Henry went to <span class='line-break'> </span> school.  Josie made<span class='line-break'> </span> Franklin some clothes.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Hubbard sent Edna <span class='line-break'> </span> and Josie a dress a<span class='line-break'> </span> peice that she had<span class='line-break'> </span> made for them.  I sewed<span class='line-break'> </span> a little on the machine<span class='line-break'> </span> for the first in several<span class='line-break'> </span> months.  I hemed<span class='line-break'> </span> a pair of sheets.<span class='line-break'> </span> There was to be a box<span class='line-break'> </span> partie at the school<span class='line-break'> </span> house to night.  It was<span class='line-break'> </span> so bad that no one went from here.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1859">
<h3><a name="page-1859">Thursday, December 23, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> helped Marvin saw wood.<span class='line-break'> </span> They got done by twelve.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim went to Chatham.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin carried him to Gretna.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben sawed wood at Johnson<span class='line-break'> </span> Reynols.  They got done by<span class='line-break'> </span> night.  Josie baked several<span class='line-break'> </span> cakes.  They looked good.<span class='line-break'> </span> I made two aprons.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry brought in<span class='line-break'> </span> some wood.  The<span class='line-break'> </span> children has bin<span class='line-break'> </span> wild to day.  They feel<span class='line-break'> </span> Xmas.  Josie and Mabel<span class='line-break'> </span> has bad colds and Edna,<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie &amp; the children<span class='line-break'> </span> shelled some pea<span class='line-break'> </span> nuts ready for roasting.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1860">
<h3><a name="page-1860">Friday, December 24, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> sawed wood at Kates<span class='line-break'> </span> and Mr Edmons.<span class='line-break'> </span> He went to Strait<span class='line-break'> </span> Stone to night.  Henry <span class='line-break'> </span> went with him.  They did<span class='line-break'> </span> not stay but a short while.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie made some cakes.<span class='line-break'> </span> She has bin complaining<span class='line-break'> </span> all day with a colde.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car sent her a present<span class='line-break'> </span> and me one two.  I got<span class='line-break'> </span> several presents today.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am glad to be remembered<span class='line-break'> </span> by the children<span class='line-break'> </span> and friends.  I am<span class='line-break'> </span> sick tonight.  Think I<span class='line-break'> </span> am taking a colde.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children has had<span class='line-break'> </span> colds.  I am sorry for<span class='line-break'> </span> them.  I was at Mr<span class='line-break'> </span> Owens a few minutes<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1861">
<h3><a name="page-1861">Saturday, December 25, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Very colde.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben staid about home<span class='line-break'> </span> all day.  The children has had<span class='line-break'> </span> a good day playing with their toys.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has a colde.  Some better<span class='line-break'> </span> to day.  I have spent the<span class='line-break'> </span> day at work.  I got breakfast,<span class='line-break'> </span> milked the cows, fed the<span class='line-break'> </span> calf, killed dressed two<span class='line-break'> </span> chickens, cooked one.  Boiled<span class='line-break'> </span> a ham, churned and <span class='line-break'> </span> beat up the butter, fixed <span class='line-break'> </span> up another churning<span class='line-break'> </span> and set it by the fire.<span class='line-break'> </span> Made some custard.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie beat the whites of <span class='line-break'> </span> the eggs for me.  Fed and <span class='line-break'> </span> watered the calf.  Brought<span class='line-break'> </span> two buckets of water.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie gave me a nice box<span class='line-break'> </span> of stationary.  Reese gave<span class='line-break'> </span> me a box of candy.  Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> gave me a nice box of stationary.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got three cards.  I was glad.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1862">
<h3><a name="page-1862">Sunday, December 26, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day and some<span class='line-break'> </span> hale and rain tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben has bin at<span class='line-break'> </span> home all day. John &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Lee and Hugh Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> was here for dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad they come.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie and I got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner. We have bin<span class='line-break'> </span> takeing things easy<span class='line-break'> </span> today. There has<span class='line-break'> </span> not bin much<span class='line-break'> </span> passing here today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Guess every body<span class='line-break'> </span> was staying at<span class='line-break'> </span> home as it is<span class='line-break'> </span> Sunday</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1863">
<h3><a name="page-1863">Monday, December 27, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A rainy morning and<span class='line-break'> </span> sleet on the <span class='line-break'> </span> ground.  Wind blowing <span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  Ben has bin at<span class='line-break'> </span> home all day.  John went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Blairs to day and<span class='line-break'> </span> Reynols is here tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin is here.  They played<span class='line-break'> </span> cards a while.<span class='line-break'> </span> We have had a good <span class='line-break'> </span> day.  As to the work did<span class='line-break'> </span> as little as we could<span class='line-break'> </span> make out with.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1864">
<h3><a name="page-1864">Tuesday, December 28, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day but very<span class='line-break'> </span> bad under foot.  John<span class='line-break'> </span> went from here this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> I hope he got home safe.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben staid at home<span class='line-break'> </span> and all the family with<span class='line-break'> </span> him.  I went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvins and spent <span class='line-break'> </span> the day.  Carrie had <span class='line-break'> </span> a good dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Heard today that Mrs<span class='line-break'> </span> Allen died last night.<span class='line-break'> </span> She had bin sick a long<span class='line-break'> </span> time.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have not seen any<span class='line-break'> </span> of the Blairs or Harvey<span class='line-break'> </span> or Reynols yet this <span class='line-break'> </span> Xmas.  Hopeful some<span class='line-break'> </span> of them will come<span class='line-break'> </span> yet.  I would like<span class='line-break'> </span> to see all of my<span class='line-break'> </span> children if I could.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1865">
<h3><a name="page-1865">Wednesday, December 29, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> family went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Jim Powers.  Ben carried<span class='line-break'> </span> 4 dogs.  Mr Power was <span class='line-break'> </span> bird huntting.  Ben hunted<span class='line-break'> </span> rabbits.  I think they<span class='line-break'> </span> all had a good day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Power was going to have <span class='line-break'> </span> a dance to night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Allen was buried<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Carrie <span class='line-break'> </span> went to work today.<span class='line-break'> </span> I staid here by my<span class='line-break'> </span> self all day.  I was<span class='line-break'> </span> busy all the morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> They say that the <span class='line-break'> </span> roads is in a bad<span class='line-break'> </span> fix.  You cant hardly<span class='line-break'> </span> get every where.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1866">
<h3><a name="page-1866">Thursday, December 30, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> hunted most of<span class='line-break'> </span> the day.  I commenced <span class='line-break'> </span> to wash and Bettie<span class='line-break'> </span> Haley come and finished<span class='line-break'> </span> for me this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Annie Doss come to get<span class='line-break'> </span> a suit case.  I let her<span class='line-break'> </span> have mine.  Tonight B<span class='line-break'> </span> carried all the family<span class='line-break'> </span> to Reynols.  Julia and<span class='line-break'> </span> her baby, Jim [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> and family, Clifton<span class='line-break'> </span> and family was there.  I was glad to<span class='line-break'> </span> see them all.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josies kids done fine<span class='line-break'> </span> for a wonder.<span class='line-break'> </span> 11 oclock</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1867">
<h3><a name="page-1867">Friday, December 31, 1920</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and family<span class='line-break'> </span> staid at home all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate and Jack Harvey<span class='line-break'> </span> come and staid a <span class='line-break'> </span> few hours.  I was glad<span class='line-break'> </span> that they come.<span class='line-break'> </span> Johnson Reynolds<span class='line-break'> </span> come a while.  I rode <span class='line-break'> </span> with him as far as<span class='line-break'> </span> Marvins.  Blair Worsham<span class='line-break'> </span> was at Marvins<span class='line-break'> </span> for some things.  I am<span class='line-break'> </span> sorry that the year is<span class='line-break'> </span> at an end and for<span class='line-break'> </span> some I am glad.  <span class='line-break'> </span> There is no telling <span class='line-break'> </span> who of us will ever<span class='line-break'> </span> see an other xmas.<span class='line-break'> </span> I hope we may all <span class='line-break'> </span> be here at next<span class='line-break'> </span> Xmas.  Good by. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
</div>
